2:28:1737:0:14:72:516:700:12:Times:12:Times:F:The Decline of Big-Bank Lending to Small Business: Dynamic Impacts on Local Credit and
2:29:1823:14:14:72:143:686:12:Times:12:Times:F:Labor Markets
2:30:1836:14:14:72:339:672:12:Times:12:Times:F:Brian S. Chen, Samuel G. Hanson, and Jeremy C. Stein
2:31:1888:14:14:72:234:658:12:Times:12:Times:F:NBER Working Paper No. 23843
2:32:1916:14:14:72:150:644:12:Times:12:Times:F:September 2017

2:34:1949:28:28:273:338:602:12:Times:12:Times:?:ABSTRACT
2:35:1957:28:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:F:Small  business  lending  by  the  four  largest  banks  fell  sharply  relative  to  others  in  2008  and 
2:36:2065:14:14:72:545:560:12:Times:12:Times:F:remained depressed  through  2014.  We  explore  the  dynamic  adjustment  process  following  this 
2:37:2164:14:14:72:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:F:credit  supply shock.  In  counties  where  the  largest  banks  had  a  high  market  share,  the  aggregate 
2:38:2273:14:14:72:546:532:12:Times:12:Times:F:flow of small business credit fell, interest rates rose, fewer businesses expanded, unemployment 
2:39:2369:14:14:71:546:518:12:Times:12:Times:F:rose,  and  wages  fell  from 2006  to  2010.  While  the  flow  of  credit  recovered  after  2010  as  other 
2:40:2479:14:14:71:546:504:12:Times:12:Times:F:lenders slowly filled the void, interest rates remain elevated. Although unemployment returns to 
2:41:2575:14:42:71:356:490:12:Times:12:Times:F:normal by 2014, the effect on wages persists in these areas.
2:42:2634:42:14:72:140:448:12:Times:12:Times:F:Brian S. Chen
2:43:2647:14:14:72:198:434:12:Times:12:Times:F:Department of Economics
2:44:2670:14:14:72:167:420:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:F:Harvard University 
2:45:2688:14:14:72:182:406:12:Times:12:g_d0_f1:F:1805 Cambridge Street

2:47:2728:14:14:72:186:378:12:Times:12:Times:F:bchen@fas.harvard.edu

3:63:2980:0:13:144:536:708:144:Times:144:Times:C:“Small business owners feel that despite being creditworthy today, banks remain 
3:64:3060:13:8:144:388:695:144:Times:144:Times:C:either wary or entirely unwilling to lend to them.” 
3:65:3112:8:13:144:146:687:36:Times:36:Times:?: 
3:66:3112:13:14:180:318:674:144:g_d0_f2:144:Times:?:Mills and McCarthy (2014). 
3:67:3138:14:22:72:75:660:144:Times:144:Times:C: 
3:68:3138:22:21:108:212:638:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:A:I. Introduction 
3:69:3153:21:20:108:543:617:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:The  above  quote  from  Karen  Mills,  the former  head  of  the  U.S.  Small  Business 
3:70:3242:20:21:72:543:597:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Administration, captures a concern expressed by many observers during the slow recovery from 
3:71:3335:21:21:72:542:576:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the 2007–2009 financial crisis and   Great Recession: t he possible existence of a small business 
3:72:3433:21:20:72:400:555:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:“credit gap”—i.e., a reduction in the supply of credit to small firms. 
3:73:3503:20:21:108:542:535:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:In this paper, we ask whether such a credit gap did in fact open up in the post-crisis period, 
3:74:3598:21:21:72:543:514:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:and what its economic implications may   have been. Our point of departure, and the basis for our 
3:75:3696:21:21:72:542:493:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:empirical strategy, is shown in Figure 1, which plots Community Reinvestment Act (CRA) data 
3:76:3788:21:20:72:542:472:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:on small business loan originations by U.S. banks. While small business lending declined at all 
3:77:3884:20:21:72:542:452:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:banks beginning in 2008, the four largest banks—those owned by Bank of America, Citigroup, 
3:78:3975:21:21:72:543:431:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:JPMorgan Chase, and Wells Fargo—cut back significantly relative to the rest of the banking 
3:79:4066:21:20:72:542:410:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:sector. By the trough in 2010, the annual flow of originations from the Top 4 banks stood at just 
3:80:4164:20:21:72:543:390:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:41% of its 2006 level, whereas the comparable figure for all other banks was 66%. Moreover, 
3:81:4256:21:21:72:543:369:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:originations at the Top 4 banks remained depressed after 2010, hovering at roughly 50% of their 
3:82:4352:21:20:72:543:348:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:pre-  crisis level through 2014. By contrast, lending at other banks slowly recovered, approaching 
3:83:4451:20:21:72:243:328:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:80% of its pre-crisis level by 2014. 
3:84:4488:21:21:108:543:307:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:We begin by arguing that this differential decline in small business lending at the Top 4 
3:85:4578:21:20:72:542:286:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:banks reflects a differential contraction in credit supply. A natural alternative is that there was a 
3:86:4680:20:21:72:542:266:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:differential shift   in credit demand, perhaps because the Top 4 were disproportionately located in 
3:87:4780:21:21:72:543:245:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:areas that were hardest hit by the Great Recession. Using CRA data   at the bank-county level, we 
3:88:4878:21:21:72:542:224:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:com pare the small business loan growth of the Top 4 banks in a given county to other banks 
3:89:4970:21:20:72:543:203:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:operating in the same county, thus sweeping away any local variation in loan demand. If anything, 
3:90:5068:20:21:72:542:183:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:these within-county differences are slightly larger in absolute magnitude than the raw across-bank 
3:91:5167:21:21:72:542:162:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:differences depicted in Figure 1, which is consistent with a supply-side rather than demand-side 
3:92:5264:21:20:72:408:141:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:explanation for the differential decline in lending at the Top 4 banks.  
3:93:5337:20:21:108:543:121:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:A harder question is why the Top 4 banks cut   their   supply of small business loans more 
3:94:5428:21:0:72:543:100:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:than other banks. Although we cannot answer this question definitively, we offer some hypotheses, 
4:95:5528:0:20:72:560:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:which we flesh out in Section II. In brief, we think of the Top 4 loan supply shift    as evolving in 
4:96:5630:20:21:72:543:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:two distinct phases. First, the Top 4 pulled backed aggressively from small business lending in 
4:97:5726:21:21:72:542:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:2008 during the midst of the financial crisis. At this time, they were experiencing high charge-off 
4:98:5826:21:20:72:543:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:rates on their small business portfolios, reinforcing their historical underperformance in a  segment 
4:99:5927:20:21:72:543:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:that they viewed as being peripheral to their overall business strategies. They also had to contend 
4:100:6027:21:21:72:564:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:with    large credit losses across a range of other products, threatening their solvency and leading to 
4:101:6131:21:20:72:543:584:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:unprecedented wholesale funding pressures. Facing these challenges, managers at large banks 
4:102:6223:20:21:72:542:564:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:chose to pull back from their non-core small business lending operations in order to focus on the 
4:103:6321:21:21:72:247:543:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:task of managing through the crisis. 
4:104:6358:21:22:108:542:522:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:In the second phase, from 2010 to 2014, the   Top 4 banks were slow to return to small 
4:105:6445:22:22:72:543:500:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:busi  ness lending once the crisis had subsided, even as smaller banks, non-bank finance companies, 
4:106:6545:22:22:72:543:478:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:and new online lenders began expanding in this market. This reluctance to re-e nter   seems to reflect 
4:107:6648:22:22:72:543:456:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:a  reassessment by the Top 4 banks of  their co  mparative advantage in the small-business segment. 
4:108:6748:22:22:72:565:434:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:And t   hese concerns may have been amplified by several post-   crisis changes in financial regulation 
4:109:6852:22:22:72:543:412:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:that weighed most heavily on the largest banks, including new capital surcharges for systemically 
4:110:6950:22:22:71:552:390:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:imp ortant institutions, the Federal Reserve’s annual bank stress-testing regime, and the  enhanced 
4:111:7050:22:22:72:290:368:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:enforcement of anti-money-laundering rules. 
4:112:7093:22:23:108:542:346:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:To be clear, we do not attempt to estimate the causal impact of  these individual channels, 
4:113:7185:23:22:72:543:323:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:much less try to  distinguish between them. Nevertheless, we believe that the above narrative makes 
4:114:7285:22:22:72:543:301:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:it all the more plausible that the decline in Top 4 lending to small business that we document can 
4:115:7384:22:22:72:549:279:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:be thought of as reflecting a systematic and sustained supply-side shift, r ather than some sort of 
4:116:7484:22:22:72:542:257:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:noise in the data.1 With this observation in hand, the remainder of the paper then focuses on 
4:117:7578:22:50:72:539:235:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:assessing the  economic  consequences  of  this shift  in credit  supply,  using a  difference-in-
4:118:7676:50:19:72:219:185:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:                                                 
4:119:7725:19:15:72:542:166:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:1In this regard, it is interesting to contrast our empirical strategy with that of Greenstone, Mas, and Nguyen (2015). 
4:120:7844:15:12:72:542:151:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:They take a more atheoretic approach, inferring that a bank has experienced an inward shift in loan supply if it has a 
4:121:7963:12:11:71:542:139:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:negative bank fixed effect in a regression of bank-county level loan growth on bank and county fixed effects. By 
4:122:8076:11:12:71:539:128:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:contrast, we are effectively requiring that the negative bank fixed effect also be accompanied by some economically-
4:123:8192:12:11:71:542:116:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:grounded priors—i.e., by a plausible story for why the bank may have cut its supply. This is why we spend a good 
4:124:8305:11:12:71:542:105:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:deal of effort trying to understand the forces underlying the Top 4 cutback in lending. The advantage of our approach 
4:125:8423:12:11:71:541:93:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:is that we are less likely to pick up bank fixed effects that amount to measurement error from the standpoint of loan 
4:126:8541:11:0:71:104:82:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:supply. 
5:127:8550:0:22:72:543:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:differences strategy that compares outcomes in counties where the Top 4 banks had a large initial 
5:128:8648:22:22:72:475:686:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:market share to those in otherwise similar counties where they had a smaller share.  
5:129:8732:22:22:108:542:664:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:We are particularly interested in understanding the dynamic impact of this contraction in 
5:130:8822:22:22:72:543:642:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:credit supply. Specifically, to the extent the pullback by the Top 4 was relatively persistent, one 
5:131:8922:22:22:72:543:620:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:would naturally expect some degree of adjustment over time both by small businesses and by other 
5:132:9019:22:22:71:557:598:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:suppliers of credit. With this dynamic perspective in mind, we first focus on county-level   outcomes 
5:133:9121:22:22:71:539:576:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:during the 2006–2010 period that covers the first phase of the Top 4’s withdrawal from small-
5:134:9214:22:22:71:542:554:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:business lending. Compared to counties with a low initial Top 4 presence, we find that counties 
5:135:9310:22:22:71:561:532:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:with a high initial Top 4 presence experience a decline in the annual flow of total    small business 
5:136:9412:22:22:71:542:510:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:lending, a decline in the fraction of business establishments that expand employment in a given 
5:137:9508:22:22:71:563:488:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:year,    slower employment growth, an increase in the  unemployment rate, and slower wage    growth. 
5:138:9609:22:23:71:542:466:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Thus, our results suggest that the credit supply shock from the Top 4 banks had a meaningful 
5:139:9702:23:22:71:542:443:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:impact on labor market outcomes in affected counties in the immediate wake of the financial crisis. 
5:140:9801:22:20:107:542:421:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:We then   explore how high Top 4 counties adapted from 2010 to 2014. We find that the 
5:141:9887:20:21:71:543:401:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:annual flow   of  small business credit to affected counties begins  to normalize after 2010 and has 
5:142:9988:21:21:71:547:380:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:largely returned to trend by 2014. We also find that the differences  in establishment expansion 
5:143:10085:21:20:71:542:359:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:rates, employment growth, and unemployment rates between high and low Top 4 counties narrow 
5:144:10177:20:21:71:542:339:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:after 2010 and largely disappear by 2014. However, we document a more persistent negative effect 
5:145:10273:21:21:71:543:318:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:on  county-level  wage  growth: the   difference between  high  and  low  Top  4  counties  remains 
5:146:10373:21:20:71:460:297:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:economically and statistically significant through the end of our sample in 2014. 
5:147:10455:20:21:107:543:277:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:In order to shed more light on these persistent wage effects, as well as on adjustment by 
5:148:10545:21:21:71:543:256:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:other lenders, we draw on proprietary data from a small business credit registry maintained by 
5:149:10640:21:21:71:543:235:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:PayNet Inc.    Using this data, we find that, beginning in 2008, small business borrowers in high Top 
5:150:10742:21:20:71:543:214:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:4 counties paid higher interest rates and obtained loans with shorter maturities. And, strikingly, 
5:151:10841:20:21:71:542:194:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:these increases in the price of small business credit persist through 2014, consistent with the idea 
5:152:10942:21:21:71:513:173:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:that small businesses have been forced to substitute towards higher cost providers of credit. 
5:153:11036:21:20:107:543:152:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:The  persistence  of  these  interest-rate  effects  helps  to  make  sense  of  our  results  for 
5:154:11135:20:21:71:570:132:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:employment and wages. Consider the consequences of a long -lived    increase in the cost of credit 
5:155:11234:21:21:71:543:111:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:in a setting where wages are sticky in the short run. Initially, higher loan rates will lead to a 
5:156:11332:21:0:71:542:90:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:temporary spike in unemployment. Then as wages gradually adjust, the effect on unemployment 
6:157:11426:0:20:72:543:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:will dissipate. However, if credit remains expensive, one would expect firms to become less capital 
6:158:11526:20:21:72:543:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:intensive over time, leading to a lower marginal product of labor. Thus, the longer-run equilibrium 
6:159:11626:21:21:72:303:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:involves a persistent negative impact on wages. 
6:160:11673:21:20:108:543:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:We next show that the composition of small business lenders in high Top 4 counties 
6:161:11756:20:21:72:543:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:changes significantly from 2008 to 2014, potentially explaining why the cost of credit remains 
6:162:11851:21:21:72:543:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:higher in these areas. As noted above, the annual flow   of small business originations by all banks 
6:163:11951:21:20:72:542:584:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:largely recovers in high Top 4 counties by 2014. This is in large part because small banks—those 
6:164:12048:20:21:72:542:564:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:with assets less than $50 billion—grow their originations faster in affected counties from 2010 to 
6:165:12147:21:21:72:543:543:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:2014, filling some   of the gap left by the Top 4 banks. Using the PayNet data, we also find that 
6:166:12245:21:21:71:543:522:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:non-bank finance companies and  alternative small business lenders—non-banks who lend via 
6:167:12335:21:20:72:542:501:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:online web-based platforms—grow most    rapidly in high Top 4 counties from 2010 to 2014. While 
6:168:12431:20:21:72:543:481:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:these non-bank lenders are responding to a legitimate shortfall in credit supply, they may be 
6:169:12525:21:21:72:543:460:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:relatively expensive marginal providers of credit, perhaps because they face higher funding costs 
6:170:12622:21:20:72:543:439:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:than banks. Thus, the adjustment process in high Top 4 counties seems to be imperfect, involving 
6:171:12719:20:21:72:339:419:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:a persistent impact on the cost of small business credit. 
6:172:12777:21:21:108:548:398:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:The validity of our   difference-in-differences approach rests on a  parallel trends assumption: 
6:173:12874:21:20:71:542:377:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:outcomes in high Top 4 counties would have evolved similarly to those in otherwise similar low 
6:174:12969:20:21:72:543:357:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Top 4 counties had the former not been hit by a  credit supply shock. In other words, we are 
6:175:13062:21:21:72:542:336:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:assuming that, conditional on a large set of controls, a county’s initial exposure to Top 4 banks is 
6:176:13163:21:20:72:542:315:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:uncorrelated with local credit demand shocks, local credit supply shocks affecting non-Top 4 
6:177:13256:20:21:72:440:295:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:lenders, and any other omitted determinants of local labor market outcomes. 
6:178:13331:21:21:108:543:274:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:We offer several pieces of evidence in support of this assumption. First, we show that 
6:179:13418:21:21:72:543:253:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:credit-market conditions and labor-market conditions evolved similarly in high and low Top 4 
6:180:13511:21:20:72:542:232:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:counties from 2000 to 2007, before diverging dramatically in 2008, precisely when the Top 4 
6:181:13603:20:21:72:562:212:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:began to aggressively pull back from small business lending. Second, we find that the    initial 
6:182:13700:21:21:72:543:191:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:decline in total small business lending in high Top 4 counties from 2006 to 2010 is entirely 
6:183:13793:21:20:72:543:170:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:explained by the Top 4 banks: smaller banks in these areas were behaving similarly to smaller 
6:184:13886:20:21:72:542:150:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:banks elsewhere. Third  , we present a series of triple-difference results that zoom in further on the 
6:185:13989:21:21:71:542:129:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:credit-supply mechanism. Looking within high Top 4 counties, we show that the employment 
6:186:14078:21:20:72:542:108:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:effects  are  concentrated  in  industries  that  are  most  dependent  on  external  finance,  such  as 
6:187:14183:20:0:72:552:88:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:manufacturing. And, looking across high Top 4 counties, we find that the  employment effects are  
7:188:14283:0:20:72:552:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:more pronounced in the subset of counties that are  most dependent on small business employers. 
7:189:14379:20:21:72:542:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Finally, our    results using the proprietary PayNet data seem uniquely consistent wi th the idea that 
7:190:14482:21:21:72:582:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:there was a credit supply shock from the Top 4 banks: the    total    volume of lending in high Top 4 
7:191:14584:21:20:72:540:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:counties declines, the cost of credit rises, and small business borrowers substitute towards non-
7:192:14681:20:21:72:543:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Top 4 lenders. Taken together, we believe that this    constellation of  findings helps to buttress the 
7:193:14785:21:21:72:269:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:validity of our basic empirical approach. 
7:194:14826:21:20:107:557:584:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Our   paper contributes  to  four    strands of the   literature. First, there is a large body of research 
7:195:14933:20:21:71:543:564:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:that studies the real effects of credit supply shocks.2 Relative to this work, our novel contribution 
7:196:15035:21:21:72:542:543:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:is to    focus less on the short   -run impact of a shock, and more on the long-run dynamic adjustment 
7:197:15138:21:21:72:543:522:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:process. Specifically, we document how labor-market outcomes like unemployment and wages 
7:198:15227:21:20:72:542:501:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:respond over time to a persistent contraction in bank loan supply, as well as how this labor-market 
7:199:15327:20:21:72:542:481:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:behavior is related to the entry of non-bank lenders. What we find most striking here is how, even 
7:200:15426:21:21:72:542:460:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:after a number of years, the process of filling in the gap left by the Top 4 banks appears to be 
7:201:15523:21:20:72:543:439:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:incomplete. This gradual adjustment process may reflect a slow -moving capital dynamic, whereby 
7:202:15619:20:21:72:543:419:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:other lenders are not easily able to raise the equity needed to expand their lending (Myers and 
7:203:15715:21:21:72:542:398:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Majluf [1984]).  Alternatively, it  may point to the importance of information-intensive banking 
7:204:15812:21:20:71:396:377:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:relationships that, once severed, are hard to rebuild (Rajan [1992]). 
7:205:15882:20:21:107:542:357:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Second,  there  is  a  set  of  papers  which  argues  that  credit  markets  played  a  role  in 
7:206:15980:21:21:72:543:336:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:precipitating and amplifying the Great Recession.3 Here our approach is particularly close to that 
7:207:16079:21:20:71:565:315:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:of  Bord, Ivashina, and Taliaferro (2017). They find   that  geographically diversified banks that were 
7:208:16183:20:21:71:540:295:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:most exposed to declining house prices cut their small business lending relative to other less-
7:209:16278:21:21:71:543:274:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:exposed banks operating in the same counties, even in those counties where real estate prices did 
7:210:16376:21:21:71:539:253:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:not fall. Thus, like us, they seek to identify a shock to small business credit supply using county-
7:211:16476:21:20:71:543:232:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:level data. One important distinction is that our strategy relies entirely on the differential behavior 
7:212:16580:20:37:71:557:212:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:of Top 4 banks versus all others, whereas their results are robust to excluding the largest ten   banks 
7:213:16684:37:19:72:219:175:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:                                                 
7:214:16733:19:15:72:546:156:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:2 Selected c ontributions include Bernanke (1983), Slovin, Sushka, and  Polonchek (1993), Peek and Rosengren (2000), 
7:215:16850:15:11:72:542:141:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Ashcraft (2005), Khwaja and Mian (2008), Schnabl (2012), Benmelech, Bergman, and Seru (2015), and Rajan and 
7:216:16958:11:10:72:151:130:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Ramcharan (2015). 
7:217:16976:10:15:72:552:120:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:3  See,  for  example, Ivashina  and  Scharfstein  (2010),  Almeida,  Campello,  Laranjeira, and    Weisbenner  (2011  ), 
7:218:17098:15:12:72:542:105:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Chodorow-Reich (2014), Mian, Rao, and Sufi (2013), Mian and Sufi (2014), Benmelech, Meisenzahl, and Ramcharan 
7:219:17208:12:11:72:542:93:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:(201 7), Greenstone, Mas, and Nguyen (2015), Duygan-Bump, Levkov, and Montoriol-Garriga (2015), Giroud and 
7:220:17315:11:0:71:235:82:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Mueller (2017), and Mondragon (2017). 
8:221:17355:0:20:72:543:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:from the analysis altogether. In this sense, the two papers study orthogonal components of the 
8:222:17450:20:21:72:543:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:overall  credit  supply  shock,  and  can  be  seen  as  complementary. It  is  useful  to  bear  this 
8:223:17553:21:21:72:543:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:complementarity in mind when thinking about the aggregate implications of both our results and 
8:224:17648:21:20:72:554:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:those of Bord et al (2017). For example, while our identification strategy leads us to focus narro  wly 
8:225:17752:20:21:72:542:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:on the relative supply shift by the Top 4 banks, we know that small business lending by all banks 
8:226:17850:21:21:72:543:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:fell dramatically in the wake of the financial crisis. If, based on evidence like that in Bord et al 
8:227:17951:21:20:71:543:584:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:(2017), one believes that some of this drop reflects a more broad-based contraction in loan supply 
8:228:18049:20:21:72:543:564:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:coming from other sources of variation, an extrapolation of our estimates and theirs would suggest 
8:229:18148:21:21:72:543:543:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:that the small business credit gap may have contributed significantly to  the   severity of the Great 
8:230:18250:21:21:71:364:522:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Recession and the sluggish pace of the subsequent recovery. 
8:231:18310:21:20:107:543:501:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Third  , to the extent that regulation played a role in the Top 4 banks’ reluctance to re-enter 
8:232:18406:20:21:71:578:481:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the small-business market once the crisis had subsided, our findings reinforce the view    that    one of 
8:233:18512:21:21:71:539:460:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the   consequences of heightened bank regulation may be to drive activity to the less-regulated, non-
8:234:18613:21:20:71:542:439:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:bank sector.4 In particular, it may be that some of the rapid growth of alternative, online lenders 
8:235:18713:20:21:72:562:419:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:in recent years is due not only   to the appeal of their web-based platforms, but also    to a simple 
8:236:18815:21:21:71:543:398:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:regulatory arbitrage: they can lend to small businesses without incurring much of the regulatory 
8:237:18912:21:20:71:301:377:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:overhead that traditional banks must shoulder.5 
8:238:18959:20:21:108:543:357:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, and most speculatively, our findings may shed some light on the weak productivity 
8:239:19050:21:21:71:581:336:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:growth in the decade since the crisis. Many authors have suggested that   some   of   the productivity 
8:240:19153:21:20:72:543:315:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:slowdown may be due to declining small business vibrancy.6 While we would not want to claim 
8:241:19244:20:21:72:542:295:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:that our results can account for the lion’s share of the productivity phenomenon—much of which 
8:242:19339:21:21:71:542:274:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:appears to be more secular in nature—it does seem possible that a contraction in bank credit supply 
8:243:19439:21:21:71:334:253:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:to small business could have played a supporting role. 
8:244:19494:21:20:107:563:232:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:The plan for the rest of the paper is as follows. In Section II, we document that    there was a 
8:245:19591:20:35:71:543:212:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:large    differential contraction in the supply of small business credit from   the    Top 4 U.S. banks 
8:246:19695:35:19:72:219:177:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:                                                 
8:247:19744:19:15:72:542:158:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:4 The potential for this unintended consequence of heightened regulation is emphasized by Acharya and Richardson 
8:248:19857:15:10:71:535:143:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:(2009), Hanson, Kashyap, and Stein (2011), Acharya, Schnabl, Suarez (2013), and Begenau and Landvoigt (2016). 
8:249:19966:10:15:72:542:133:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:5 Relatedly, Buchak, Matvos, Piskorski, and   Seru   (2017) show that non-bank lenders have also gained significant 
8:250:20082:15:11:71:542:118:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:market share in residential mortgage lending since the financial crisis, and they present evidence linking the rise of 
8:251:20201:11:10:71:433:107:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:non-   bank mortgage lenders to the heightened regulations now faced by traditional banks.  
8:252:20292:10:15:72:542:97:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:6 See, for instance, Decker, Haltiwanger, Jarmin and Miranda (2014), Hathaway and Litan (2014), Haltiwanger, 
8:253:20401:15:0:71:303:82:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Hathaway, and Miranda (2014), and Haltiwanger (2015). 
9:254:20456:0:20:72:543:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:beginning in 2008 and continuing through 2014; we also discuss some of the possible causes of 
9:255:20550:20:21:72:543:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:this pullback. Section III  explains our identification strategy for assessing the dynamic impact of 
9:256:20651:21:21:72:552:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:this  supply shock on local    credit and labor markets. Section IV details the  data sources we use in 
9:257:20755:21:20:71:547:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the analysis. Section V describes our principal empirical results, and Section VI of fers some 
9:258:20850:20:21:71:172:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:concluding remarks. 
9:259:20870:21:14:71:74:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B: 
9:260:20870:14:21:107:521:591:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:A:II. Contraction in the Supply of Small Business Loans from the Top 4 Banks 
9:261:20943:21:20:107:345:570:144:Times:144:Times:A:A. Identifying the relative shock to credit supply 
9:262:20993:20:21:107:539:550:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:As noted above, and as can be seen in Figure 1 and Panel A of Table 1, the Top 4 banks—
9:263:21080:21:21:72:542:529:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:those owned by Bank of America, Citigroup, JP Morgan, and Wells Fargo—significantly cut their 
9:264:21174:21:20:72:543:508:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:small business lending relative to other U.S.    banks beginning in 2008. We first demonstrate that 
9:265:21274:20:21:72:543:488:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:this is truly a big bank effect: the    reduction in lending by the Top 4 goes beyond what one would 
9:266:21375:21:21:72:543:467:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:expect based on their other observable characteristics. To see this, Panel A of Table 2 presents 
9:267:21472:21:24:72:320:446:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:bank-level  , cross-sectional regressions of the form: 
9:268:21526:24:25:109:543:422:175:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:%4.bbbbLoansTαβε′∆    =+×  +  +γx (1) 
9:269:21563:25:22:108:543:397:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:The dependent variable in equation (1) is    the percentage point change in bank b’s small 
9:270:21654:22:21:72:542:375:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:business loan originations from 2006 to 2010. We are interested in the coefficient β on the indicator 
9:271:21756:21:20:71:542:354:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:for   Top 4 banks, denoted T4b. Column (1) reports the coefficient from a univariate regression of 
9:272:21855:20:21:72:542:334:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:2006–2010 origination growth on the Top 4 indicator. The estimate implies that small business 
9:273:21949:21:21:72:556:313:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:lending by the Top 4 fell by 31.6 percentage points (“p.p.”) relative to other banks. In c  olumn (2), 
9:274:22051:21:21:71:543:292:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:we control for a set of bank-level   characteristics from the Call Reports, including a bank’s funding 
9:275:22154:21:20:71:543:271:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:mix (its fraction of deposit funding and its fraction of wholesale funding), pre-crisis asset growth, 
9:276:22256:20:21:71:543:251:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:C&I charge-offs during the crisis, exposure to real estate loans, and initial equity capital ratios. 
9:277:22357:21:21:71:543:230:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:The inclusion of these controls has only a small effect on the   coefficient on the Top 4 indicator 
9:278:22456:21:20:72:191:209:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:which falls to –26.4 p.p. 
9:279:22482:20:21:108:542:189:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:We next compare the Top 4 banks to “small banks”—those with assets under $50 billion 
9:280:22567:21:21:72:543:168:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:in 2005—and “other larger banks” excluding the Top 4—those with 2005 assets between $50 
9:281:22655:21:20:72:543:147:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:billion and $500 billion. To do so, in columns (3) and (4), we include indicator variables for both 
9:282:22755:20:21:72:543:127:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the Top 4 and for other large banks A50to500b, so small banks serve as the omitted category. The 
9:283:22852:21:21:71:542:106:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:estimates in column (4) imply that, all else equal, the originations of the Top 4 shrank by 38.2 p.p. 
9:284:22954:21:0:71:543:85:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:relative to small banks, while those of other large banks fell by 15.4 p.p. relative to small banks. 
10:285:23057:0:20:72:543:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Furthermore, the 22.8 p.p. difference between the Top 4 and other large banks is large in magnitude 
10:286:23156:20:21:72:542:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:and statistically significant at the 1% level. Thus, columns (3) and (4) suggest that while the 
10:287:23252:21:21:72:543:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:contraction in small business lending is a function of bank size more generally, the very largest 
10:288:23350:21:20:72:542:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:banks—the Top 4—withdrew by considerably more than even “super-regional” banks with assets 
10:289:23441:20:21:72:221:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:between $50 and $500 billion. 
10:290:23471:21:21:108:542:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:What explains these differences? One possibility is that they reflect differences in loan 
10:291:23561:21:20:72:549:584:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:demand, or in  borrower creditworthiness, as opposed to differential changes in credit supply. For  
10:292:23661:20:21:72:540:564:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:example, Figure 2 shows the geographic distribution of the Top 4 deposit share in a given market—
10:293:23758:21:21:71:542:543:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:denoted  by T4DSc—across counties  in  the  lower  48  states.  The  population-weighted average 
10:294:23855:21:21:71:542:522:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:county has a T4DSc of 30%. However, there are clear regional patterns in Top 4 presence, with 
10:295:23949:21:20:72:542:501:144:Times:144:g_d0_f2:B:T4DSc averaging 25% in the Northeast census region, 29% in the South, 15% in the Midwest, and 
10:296:24043:20:21:72:542:481:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:50% in the West. Since T4DSc is not randomly distributed across regions, our findings in Panel A 
10:297:24140:21:21:72:543:460:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:of Table 2 could just be capturing the   fact that the Top 4 operated in areas that were harder hit by 
10:298:24243:21:20:72:457:439:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the Great Recession and, therefore, experienced larger declines in loan demand. 
10:299:24322:20:21:108:542:419:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:To address this concern, in Panel B of Table 2, we use CRA data on small business loan 
10:300:24409:21:24:71:435:398:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f4:B:originations at the bank-county level to estimate specifications of the form: 
10:301:24486:24:26:109:543:374:175:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:%4,bccbbbcLoansTαβε′∆= +×  +  +γx (2) 
10:302:24523:26:21:72:543:348:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:where %Δ 퐿퐿퐿퐿퐿퐿퐿퐿퐿퐿푏푏푏푏 is the percentage point change in bank b’s small business loan originations in 
10:303:24625:21:21:72:542:327:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:county c. B ecause equation (2) includes county fixed effects, our estimates are now identified using 
10:304:24727:21:20:72:542:306:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:only   wit  hin-  county variation in origination growth across banks. This means that our estimates are 
10:305:24832:20:21:71:371:286:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:not influenced by differences in loan demand across counties. 
10:306:24893:21:21:107:568:265:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Interestingly, the estimated coefficients on T4b in Panel B are similar to the raw  a cross   -
