10:310:25292:21:20:71:542:182:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:emphasize below, the fact that the estimates in Panels A and B of Table 2 are similar helps to 
10:311:25387:20:21:71:542:162:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:bolster  the key   parallel  trends  assumption  that  we make when we  examine  the  economic 
10:312:25481:21:21:71:396:141:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:consequences of the Top 4’s pullback from small business lending. 
10:313:25547:21:0:215:218:120:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:?:  
11:314:25549:0:20:108:402:708:144:Times:144:Times:A:B. Why did credit supply contract more at the Top 4 banks? 
11:315:25607:20:21:108:543:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:If we stipulate that there was indeed a relative shift in credit supply, why did the Top 4 cut 
11:316:25702:21:21:72:562:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:their supply of small business loans more    aggressively than other banks in 2008? And why didn’t 
11:317:25801:21:20:72:542:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the Top 4 return to this market once the financial crisis subsided, even as other lenders did so? 
11:318:25899:20:21:72:543:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:While we are not able to provide decisive answers  to these questions, we    are able to delineate a 
11:319:26000:21:21:72:543:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:few hypotheses about the origins of the credit supply shock, based on our reading of various written 
11:320:26100:21:20:72:543:584:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:accounts, as well as a series of conservations with bank executives, financial industry consultants, 
11:321:26201:20:27:72:167:564:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:and policymakers.7 
11:322:26219:27:21:108:344:537:144:Times:144:Times:A:B.1. Phase 1: The initial pullback, 2008-2010 
11:323:26264:21:21:108:543:516:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Observers offer    a consistent story to explain the Top 4’s withdrawal from small business 
11:324:26356:21:20:72:542:495:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:lending in 2008. Prior to the crisis, this segment was only a modest portion of the Top 4’s total 
11:325:26454:20:21:72:542:475:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:loan portfolios. For instance, based on mid  -2006 Call Report data, small business loans represented 
11:326:26556:21:21:72:559:454:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:only   4% of total outstanding loans at the Top 4, compared to 9%   of loans at other large banks with 
11:327:26659:21:20:72:543:433:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:assets between $50 and $500 billion, and 22% of loans at small banks with assets under $50 billion. 
11:328:26759:20:21:72:543:413:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:This pattern has been rationalized by noting that, relative to smaller banks, large banks are at a 
11:329:26857:21:21:72:543:392:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:disadvantage in gathering and  acting on the kind of non-quantitative, “soft” information that is so 
11:330:26958:21:20:72:542:371:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:useful when assessing the creditworthiness of small firms    (Stein [2002], Berger and Udell [2002], 
11:331:27059:20:21:72:542:351:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Berger, Miller, Petersen, Rajan, and Stein [2005], Liberti and Mian [2009], and Berger, Bouwman, 
11:332:27156:21:21:72:158:330:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:and Kim [2017]). 
11:333:27173:21:20:108:542:309:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:However,  from   2000 to  2007, large  banks  began  relying  more  heavily  on  automated 
11:334:27264:20:21:72:549:289:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:systems—similar to those used  in consumer and residential mortgage lending—to underwrite 
11:335:27354:21:21:72:543:268:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:small  business  loans based  solely  on  quantitative,  “hard”  information (Carroll  and  Hoffman 
11:336:27454:21:21:72:542:247:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:[2013],  Mills  and  McCarthy  [2014]).  These  automated underwriting systems  combined 
11:337:27543:21:20:72:543:226:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:information on the business owner’s consumer credit score and, where available, a commercial 
11:338:27636:20:21:72:542:206:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:credit score. The hope was that moving to an automated system would lower processing costs and 
11:339:27731:21:59:72:542:185:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:improve underwriting quality. With the aid of   these automated systems, the Top 4 banks gained 
11:340:27827:59:18:72:219:126:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:                                                 
11:341:27876:18:0:72:516:108:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:7 See, for example, “Big banks cut back on loans to small business,” Wall Street Journal, November 26, 2015. 
12:342:27987:0:20:72:542:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:meaningful shar  e in the small business market in the years leading up the crisis, going from 
12:343:28082:20:21:72:366:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:approximately 20% of originations in 2000 to 33% in 2006.8 
12:344:28140:21:21:108:542:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:But as the U.S. economy decelerated from mid-2007 to late    2008, big banks experienced 
12:345:28229:21:20:71:543:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:high charge-off   rates on their small business loan portfolios. Furthermore, they realized that the 
12:346:28330:20:21:71:543:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:transition to automated underwriting had not significantly lowered costs or improved underwriting 
12:347:28428:21:24:71:386:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:quality.9 For example, according to Mills and McCarthy (2014):  
12:348:28492:24:14:108:545:581:144:Times:144:Times:A:“Bank  of  America,  which  used  credit  scoring  to  make  ...  loans  of  less  than  $150,000  
12:349:28591:14:13:108:543:567:144:Times:144:Times:A:through 2007, suffered significant losses in the recession and eventually exited that market 
12:350:28684:13:23:108:515:554:144:Times:144:Times:A:segment due in part to poor loans underwritten largely based on credit score data.” 
12:351:28768:23:21:108:543:531:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:By   lat e 2008, the Top 4 banks were facing huge losses in their core lending and capital 
12:352:28859:21:21:71:543:510:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:markets divisions, threatening their solvency and leading to intense wholesale funding pressures. 
12:353:28956:21:20:72:542:489:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Executives at these banks needed to stabilize core    business lines, rebuild equity capital buffers, 
12:354:29058:20:21:71:542:469:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:and pass the U.S. government’s May    2009 stress test. Facing these challenges, the large banks 
12:355:29155:21:21:71:540:448:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:pull  ed back from small business lending—a non-core unit where they were already struggling—
12:356:29248:21:23:71:512:427:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:to focus on weathering the storm.10 For example, according to Mills and McCarthy (2014): 
12:357:29337:23:14:108:542:404:144:Times:144:Times:A:“Some banks, particularly larger banks... significantly reduced or eliminated loans below 
12:358:29427:14:14:108:543:390:144:Times:144:Times:A:a certain threshold, typically $100,000 or $250,000, or simply [would] not lend to small 
12:359:29516:14:23:108:359:376:144:Times:144:Times:A:businesses with revenue of less than $2 million ....” 
12:360:29570:23:20:108:542:353:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:To illustrate the economic logic behind this sort of decision, consider a stylized example 
12:361:29661:20:21:72:542:333:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:with    two banks, where Bank A is a mid  -size  regional player primarily involved in traditional 
12:362:29760:21:21:71:542:312:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:commercial banking activities, while Bank B is a Top 4 megabank that also is involved in a wide 
12:363:29856:21:20:71:542:291:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:range of other capital markets and investment banking lines of business. Now suppose both banks 
12:364:29952:20:21:71:543:271:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:see the profitability of their small-bus iness lending unit decline by the same amount due to changes 
12:365:30054:21:21:71:543:250:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:in  the  macroeconomic  environment  or increased regulation. Even  in  the  face  of  this  sort  of 
12:366:30156:21:29:71:542:229:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:symmetric shock, which bank might be expected to cut back on small business lending by more? 
12:367:30249:29:19:72:219:200:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:                                                 
12:368:30298:19:15:72:542:181:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:8 We calculate market share using CRA data. To ensure comparability over time, we adjust the historical series for all 
12:369:30417:15:11:72:551:166:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:subsequent acquisitions by the Top 4 banks. Furthermore, since the bank   asset size threshold for CRA reporting 
12:370:30530:11:12:71:542:155:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:increased from $250 million in 2004 to $1 billion in 2005, we exclude banks with fewer than $1 billion in assets before 
12:371:30650:12:10:71:116:143:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:2005.     
12:372:30660:10:15:72:542:133:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:9 Processing costs did not fall much because large banks only used automatic systems to decide the most obvious cases 
12:373:30778:15:11:72:542:118:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:and continued to use a high-cost, manual process to decide the rest. And, underwriting quality did not improve because 
12:374:30897:11:10:72:532:107:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:automated models were not particularly good at forecasting small business defaults (Carroll and Hoffman [2013]). 
12:375:31009:10:15:72:547:97:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:10  Observers  told  us  that  the  large  banks  mostly  shut  down  their  automated  underwriting  systems,  routed  all 
12:376:31133:15:0:71:473:82:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:applications through their manual systems, and significantly tightened their underwriting standards. 
13:377:31236:0:20:72:543:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Assuming that banks don’t return capital to shareholders—so that their capital base is fixed in the 
13:378:31336:20:21:72:543:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:short run—it should be megabank B. Megabank B has a broader set of other available opportunities 
13:379:31433:21:21:72:543:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:in its internal capital market to which it can reallocate capital if it exits small business lending. By 
13:380:31538:21:20:72:542:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:contrast, for the regional bank A, it is harder to exit small business lending if it wants to maintain 
13:381:31641:20:27:72:546:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:its   current size,    because it faces a more limited set of opportunities in reallocating capital internally.  
13:382:31754:27:21:108:336:599:144:Times:144:Times:A:B.2. Phase 2: The slow rebound, 2010-2014 
13:383:31795:21:20:108:543:578:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:As shown in Table 1, small business lending at the Top 4 banks rebounded modestly after 
13:384:31883:20:21:72:543:558:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:2010,  growing by  19%  from  2010  to  2014. However,  since the  Top  4  had  cut lending so 
13:385:31978:21:21:72:542:537:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:aggressively from 2006 to 2010, one might have expected a stronger recovery. Indeed, originations 
13:386:32076:21:21:72:552:516:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:grew by 34% from 2010 to 2014 at small banks with assets under $50 billion, even though they  
13:387:32170:21:20:72:262:495:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:had cut lending by far less in the crisis. 
13:388:32212:20:21:108:543:475:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Several factors may    help to explain why the Top 4 did not jump back into small business 
13:389:32303:21:21:72:543:454:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:lending once the crisis had passed. One    possibility is that the rapid growth in small business 
13:390:32401:21:20:72:542:433:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:lending at the Top 4 banks in the years prior to the crisis was a boom-time over-extension of 
13:391:32495:20:21:72:542:413:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:credit—something akin to what occurred in the residential mortgage sector, albeit on a much 
13:392:32587:21:21:72:543:392:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:smaller scale. And, having been disappointed with their ill-fated expansion into small business 
13:393:32683:21:20:72:539:371:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:credit and particularly their foray into automated underwriting, the largest banks permanently re-
13:394:32781:20:21:72:543:351:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:evaluated  their  comparat ive    advantage  in  this  area  following  the  crisis.  In  this  telling, while 
13:395:32892:21:21:72:543:330:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:perhaps painful, the post-2007 decline in small business lending at the Top 4 banks was a necessary 
13:396:32991:21:20:72:257:309:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:corrective to these pre-crisis excesses. 
13:397:33031:20:21:108:539:289:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Another possibility is that the slow rebound was in part a consequence of heightened post-
13:398:33121:21:21:72:543:268:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:crisis financial regulation. Even as late as 2014, a significant fraction of senior managers’ time at 
13:399:33223:21:21:72:543:247:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the  largest  banks  was  being  consumed  by  the  need  to  comply  with  the  array  of  heightened 
13:400:33326:21:20:71:542:226:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:regulations that had gone into effect following the crisis—Basel III’s new capital and liquidity 
13:401:33423:20:21:71:551:206:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:rules, the Federal Reserve’s annual bank stress tests, the preparation of so-called “living wills,”  to 
13:402:33527:21:21:71:542:185:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:name   but    a few. This left less bandwidth to devote to the task of reimagining a struggling peripheral 
13:403:33634:21:20:71:289:164:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:business line such as small business lending. 
13:404:33679:20:21:107:543:144:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:More directly, in the wake of the crisis, effective capital requirements have gone up not 
13:405:33769:21:21:71:543:123:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:only in absolute terms, but also by more for the very    largest banks. Those  banks that are deemed 
13:406:33870:21:0:71:543:102:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:to be globally systemically significant, such as the Top 4 banks, face capital surcharges, forcing 
14:407:33972:0:20:72:543:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:them to maintain higher capital ratios against all  risky assets relative to other banks.11 Moreover, 
14:408:34074:20:21:72:543:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the implicit risk weights for small business loans in particular may have increased at large banks 
14:409:34173:21:21:72:543:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:in recent years. This would be the case to the extent that the   stress  -testing regime that the Federal 
14:410:34279:21:20:71:542:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Reserve now applies to banks with assets over $50 billion make   s  relatively severe assumptions 
14:411:34377:20:21:71:543:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:about the losses on small business loans in  an  economic downturn.12 While heightened capital 
14:412:34472:21:21:71:542:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:charges are arguably a well   -justified component of the post-crisis efforts to reduce the systemic 
14:413:34573:21:20:71:542:584:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:risk posed by the very largest banks, they may have some chilling effect on the amount of riskier 
14:414:34671:20:21:71:366:564:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:lending—e.g., small business lending—done by these banks. 
14:415:34729:21:21:107:543:543:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, it is possible that Know Your Customer (KYC) regulations may    have played a role 
14:416:34820:21:21:72:542:522:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:as well. Loosely speaking, these rules require banks to verify their customers’ identities and to 
14:417:34918:21:20:71:543:501:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:monitor their activi   ty for suspicious transactions, with the aim of reducing financial fraud and 
14:418:35018:20:21:71:543:481:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:money laundering. Some observers have suggested that the enforcement of these rules, and the 
14:419:35111:21:21:71:540:460:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:size of the associated penalties, have become tougher for big banks, in comparison to both   the pre-
14:420:35212:21:20:71:543:439:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:crisis    period and to smaller banks. KYC compliance costs are incurred when a bank enters into 
14:421:35309:20:21:71:543:419:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:any relationship with a small business, and are not specific to just len ding. Yet    to the extent that 
14:422:35414:21:21:71:530:398:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:they are meaningful, they might be expected to affect the economics of small business lending. 
14:423:35509:21:20:107:542:377:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Given  the  short  time  series  we  are  unable  to  distinguish  between  these  competing 
14:424:35602:20:21:71:542:357:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:explanations for  the post-crisis decline in small business lending at the Top 4 banks. That is, we 
14:425:35702:21:21:71:542:336:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:cannot say whether it was an unintended consequence of heightened regulation or a return to the 
14:426:35798:21:20:71:539:315:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:normal, pre-boom state of affairs. However, we will  argue that one particular aspect of the credit-
14:427:35898:20:21:71:542:295:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:boom story  —that high Top 4 counties had a larger aggregate increase in small business lending 
14:428:35994:21:21:71:496:274:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:than low Top 4 counties in the pre-crisis period—appears to be unsupported in the data. 
14:429:36082:21:21:107:110:253:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A: 
14:430:36082:21:22:107:110:232:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A: 
14:431:36082:22:19:72:219:210:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:                                                 
14:432:36131:19:15:72:547:191:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:11 Specifically,  since the Top 4 banks qualify as Global Systemically Important Banks (GSIBs), they are required  to 
14:433:36249:15:12:71:544:176:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:have   additional Tier 1 common equity relative to risk-weighted assets. The current surcharges are 3.5% for JP M organ, 
14:434:36370:12:10:71:371:164:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:3% for C   itigroup, 3% for B ank of America, and 2% for Wells   Fargo . 
14:435:36443:10:15:72:542:154:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:12 An important qualification is that we cannot observe these stress-test loss assumptions separately for small business 
14:436:36564:15:11:71:542:139:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:loans as opposed to the broader category of all commercial and industrial lending. See however The Clearing House 
14:437:36678:11:12:71:542:128:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:(2017) for an analysis that attempts to indirectly infer the stress-test implied risk weights on small-business loans. 
14:438:36797:12:11:71:542:116:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:Going further, several observers with ties to the financial industry have argued that the tougher bank capital regulations 
14:439:36920:11:12:71:541:105:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:adopted in the wake of the crisis have contributed to the slow growth of small business lending, particularly at the 
14:440:37037:12:11:71:542:93:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:largest banks, potentially helping to explain why employment growth at small firms has lagged behind that at larger 
14:441:37153:11:0:71:542:82:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:firms during the post-crisis recovery. See, for example, The Clearing House (2017) and Strongin et al. (2014, 2015).  
15:442:37273:0:20:108:531:708:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:A:III. Assessing the Economic Consequences: Empirical Strategy and Predictions 
15:443:37348:20:21:108:542:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:To   assess the   impact of the credit supply shock on local credit and labor markets, we use a 
15:444:37444:21:21:72:542:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:difference-in-difference strategy that compares outcomes in counties where the Top 4 banks had a 
15:445:37541:21:20:72:543:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:large   r  initial market share to those in observably similar counties where they had a smaller share. 
15:446:37644:20:28:72:405:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:This   empirical strategy rests on two key identifying assumptions: 
15:447:37712:28:16:90:542:598:144:g_d0_f7:144:Times:A:• First stage assumption: Because of the relative credit supply shift from the Top 4 banks, 
15:448:37803:16:16:108:542:582:144:Times:144:Times:A:a county’s initial Top 4 share is negatively related to the subsequent growth in aggregate 
15:449:37894:16:23:108:297:566:144:Times:144:g_d0_f2:A:small business lending in that county. 
15:450:37932:23:15:89:543:543:144:g_d0_f7:144:Times:A:• Parallel trends / Exclusion restriction assumption: Conditional on a set of county-level 
15:451:38022:15:16:108:543:528:144:Times:144:Times:A:observables, a county’s initial Top 4 share is uncorrelated with (i) local credit demand 
15:452:38111:16:16:108:547:512:144:Times:144:Times:A:shocks,  (ii)  local  credit  supply  shocks  affecting  other  lenders,  and  (iii)  omitted  
15:453:38206:16:16:108:543:496:144:Times:144:Times:A:determinants  of  local  real  outcomes.  Thus,  credit  and  labor  market  outcomes  in  high  
15:454:38303:16:16:108:543:480:144:Times:144:Times:A:and low Top 4 counties would have evolved similarly in the absence of the relative credit 
15:455:38393:16:22:108:286:464:144:Times:144:g_d0_f2:A:supply shock from the Top 4 banks. 
15:456:38427:22:20:72:542:442:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Assuming that these identifying assumptions hold, then our difference-in-difference estimates will 
15:457:38526:20:21:72:239:422:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:have a valid causal interpretation.  
15:458:38562:21:21:108:543:401:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:We    test  four difference-in-difference (DD)   predictions  in  the  cross-section  of  U.S. 
15:459:38657:21:27:72:118:380:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:counties: 
15:460:38667:27:16:90:542:353:144:g_d0_f7:144:Times:A:• Prediction DD1: There is a negative relationship between a county’s initial Top 4 share 
15:461:38756:16:23:108:519:337:144:Times:144:Times:A:and the subsequent growth in total small business loan originations in that county. 
15:462:38839:23:16:90:542:314:144:g_d0_f7:144:Times:A:• Prediction DD2: There is a negative relationship between a county’s initial Top 4 share 
15:463:38928:16:16:108:542:298:144:Times:144:Times:A:and  subsequent  county-level labor-market  outcomes,  including  employment and  wage 
15:464:39015:16:21:108:151:282:144:Times:144:g_d0_f2:A:growth.  
15:465:39023:21:21:72:543:261:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Note that by combining Predictions DD1    and DD2, we can    obtain an instrumental-variables (IV) 
15:466:39122:21:28:72:484:240:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:estimate of the impact of a small business credit supply shock on local labor markets. 
15:467:39209:28:16:90:547:212:144:g_d0_f7:144:Times:A:• Prediction DD3: There is a positive relationship between a county’s   initial Top 4 share 
15:468:39300:16:21:108:509:196:144:Times:144:g_d0_f2:A:and subsequent changes in interest rates on small business loans in that county.  
15:469:39381:21:21:108:542:175:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Combining Predictions DD1 and DD3 yields an IV estimate of semi-elasticity of loan 
15:470:39464:21:21:72:542:154:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:demand with respect to interest rates. Although we primarily focus on results from reduced-form 
15:471:39560:21:21:72:543:133:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:specifications, we take comfort from the fact that the corresponding IV estimate—the ratio of 
15:472:39654:21:20:72:539:112:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:coefficients from the reduced-form and the first-stage specifications—implies a plausible semi-
15:473:39749:20:0:72:293:92:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:elasticity of demand for small business loans. 
16:474:39799:0:15:90:542:707:144:g_d0_f7:144:Times:A:• Prediction DD4: There is a positive relationship between a county’s initial Top 4 share 
16:475:39888:15:16:108:543:692:144:Times:144:Times:A:and subsequent small business loan growth for other, non-Top 4 lenders in that county, 
16:476:39975:16:22:108:430:676:144:Times:144:Times:A:including smaller banks, finance companies, and online lenders. 
16:477:40038:22:21:72:543:654:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Combining Predictions DD3 and DD4, we can obtain an IV estimate of the semi-elasticity of loan 
16:478:40133:21:20:71:542:633:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:supply for these other lenders. And, as above, we will draw comfort from the fact that the implied 
16:479:40232:20:21:72:298:613:144:g_d0_f2:144:Times:B:semi   -elasticity of loan supply seems plausible. 
16:480:40282:21:21:108:543:592:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:In addition, finding evidence consistent with Predictions DD3 and DD4 supports the view 
16:481:40370:21:21:72:542:571:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:that   any  negative impact on local    economic outcomes such as business growth and employment is 
16:482:40470:21:20:71:543:550:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:due to a  Top 4 credit supply shock rather than to  a failure of the exclusion restriction. For example, 
16:483:40575:20:21:71:542:530:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:suppose one is  worried that a county’s initial Top 4 share is correlated with negative shocks to 
16:484:40673:21:21:72:542:509:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:local economic fundamentals and, thus, to loan demand, which could explain why Predictions DD1 
16:485:40768:21:20:72:543:488:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:and DD2 hold in the data. In this case, we would also expect to find a decline in interest rates and 
16:486:40869:20:21:72:423:468:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:slower loan growth at other non-Top 4 lenders in high Top 4 counties.13  
16:487:40942:21:21:108:542:447:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:However, even if we do find   evidence supporting each of  Predictions DD1 through DD4, 
16:488:41030:21:20:72:543:426:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:one    may    still ask whether exposure to the   Top 4 banks impacts local   labor market outcomes 
16:489:41130:20:21:72:543:406:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:through a narrow small business credit supply channel of the sort we have in mind, or through a 
16:490:41226:21:21:72:542:385:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:broader credit supply channel. The small business credit channel is the idea that an inward shift in 
16:491:41327:21:20:72:543:364:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the supply of credit to small    businesses had a direct negative impact on local labor markets.14 
16:492:41425:20:21:72:566:344:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:However, there may also be a broader credit channel because, while the  Top 4 cut  their    lending to 
16:493:41528:21:21:71:542:323:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:small businesses sharply beginning in 2008, their loan growth has also been stagnant in other 
16:494:41622:21:21:72:543:302:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:categories, including residential mortgage and consumer lending. So a contraction in  the  supply of 
16:495:41723:21:20:72:543:281:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:household credit from   Top 4 banks may also    have reduced consumer demand in affected counties, 
16:496:41822:20:21:72:543:261:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:leading to adverse effects on local    employment even in the absence of a direct small business credit 
16:497:41926:21:30:72:115:240:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:channel. 
16:498:41935:30:19:72:219:210:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:                                                 
16:499:41984:19:15:72:542:191:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:13 When considering the impact on interest rates, it is important to  hold expected default losses constant.  Otherwise, 
16:500:42105:15:12:71:542:176:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:if weak local fundamentals were associated with higher expected credit losses, one might expect a county with poor 
16:501:42220:12:11:71:554:164:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:fundamentals to have both   low loan growth and higher raw interest rates. Thus, we take care to control for loan credit 
16:502:42341:11:10:71:322:153:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:quality (measured by the average credit score) in each county. 
16:503:42404:10:15:72:542:143:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:14 Of course, the impact on labor markets is unlikely to be caused exclusively by an inward shift in the supply of 
16:504:42519:15:12:71:542:128:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:business loans with amounts less than $1 million—the literal regulatory definition of small business loans. If the Top 
16:505:42638:12:11:71:549:116:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:4 are cutting back on their supply of business loans less than $1 million, then they are  also likely to be cutting back 
16:506:42759:11:12:71:542:105:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:on their supply of loans between $1 and $20 million to medium-sized businesses. Indeed, based on data on outstanding 
16:507:42876:12:11:71:542:93:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:commercial  loan  balances  from  Call  Reports,  we find    that  commercial  loan  growth  at  the  Top  4  has lagged 
16:508:42997:11:0:71:542:82:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:significantly behind that at smaller banks—both for loans under $1 million and for loans over $1 million—since 2007. 
17:509:43116:0:20:108:551:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:To help distinguish between these stories, we use triple-difference specifications to   test 
17:510:43209:20:28:72:522:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:three   further predictions that are unique to the narrower small business credit supply channel: 
17:511:43307:28:16:90:542:660:144:g_d0_f7:144:Times:A:• Prediction DDD1: Looking across high Top 4 counties, the negative employment effects 
17:512:43393:16:16:108:542:644:144:Times:144:Times:A:should be most pronounced in the subset of counties that were initially more dependent 
17:513:43480:16:22:108:254:628:144:Times:144:g_d0_f4:A:on small business employers. 
17:514:43508:22:16:90:542:606:144:g_d0_f7:144:Times:A:• Prediction DDD2: Looking within high Top 4 counties, the negative employment effects 
17:515:43594:16:22:108:519:590:144:Times:144:g_d0_f2:A:should be concentrated in industries that are more dependent on external finance.  
17:516:43675:22:21:72:542:568:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Importantly, Prediction DDD2 can be tested exploiting only within-county variation. This helps 
17:517:43770:21:20:72:543:547:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:address any concerns about the failure of the exclusion restriction due to unobserved differential 
17:518:43869:20:21:72:225:527:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:demand trends across counties. 
17:519:43899:21:21:108:542:506:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Furthermore, since small firm s in tradable industries such as manufacturing tend to be more 
17:520:43992:21:21:71:543:485:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:reliant on external finance than small firms in non-tradable industries like    retail and restaurants, 
17:521:44096:21:27:72:427:464:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:this  suggests that our employment results should be stronger in tradables: 
17:522:44172:27:16:90:542:437:144:g_d0_f7:144:Times:A:• Prediction DDD3: Looking within high Top 4 counties, the negative employment effects 
17:523:44258:16:22:108:435:421:144:Times:144:g_d0_f2:A:should be stronger in tradable industries such as manufacturing.  
17:524:44322:22:20:72:542:399:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:And given that employment in tradables is less exposed to shifts in local demand than employment 
17:525:44419:20:21:71:543:379:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:in non-tradables (Mian and Sufi [2014]), finding evidence in favor of Prediction DDD3 would cut 
17:526:44515:21:21:71:543:358:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:against an interpretation of our results in which credit-induced shifts in household demand play a 
17:527:44614:21:27:71:127:337:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:major role. 
17:528:44626:27:20:71:74:310:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B: 
17:529:44626:20:21:107:214:290:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:A:IV. Data Sources 
17:530:44642:21:21:107:546:269:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:We carry out much of  our analysis using a panel data set that consists of annual, county-
17:531:44732:21:32:71:528:248:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:level observations. This section describes the main data sources we use to construct this panel. 
17:532:44829:32:21:107:262:216:144:Times:144:Times:A:A. Small business lending data 
17:533:44859:21:21:107:551:195:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Our data on  small business loan originations in each U.S. county are  derived from the 
17:534:44947:21:20:71:543:174:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Community Reinvestment Act (CRA) database. Any federally-regulated depository institution 
17:535:45037:20:21:71:543:154:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:whose assets exceed $1 billion in  2005 dollars is required to file a CRA report. Small business 
17:536:45134:21:21:71:548:133:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:loans are loans    with an original amount of $1 million or less that   are reported as either “c ommercial 
17:537:45242:21:21:71:543:112:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:and industrial loans” or    “loans secured by nonfarm or nonresidential real estate” on an institution’s 
17:538:45347:21:0:71:542:91:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Call  Report. The concept of originations in the CRA database includes renewals and refinancings 
18:539:45447:0:20:72:543:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:as well as de novo ori ginations. Furthermore, the data includes both term loans and credit line 
18:540:45542:20:21:72:479:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:approvals. In the latter case, the origination amount equals the size of the credit line. 
18:541:45631:21:21:108:542:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:We obtain data on lending terms, as well as on lending volumes by non-bank finance 
18:542:45714:21:20:71:542:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:companies and online lenders, from   PayNet’s proprietary loan-level database. PayNet maintains a 
18:543:45812:20:21:71:543:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:private business credit registry that aggregates and analyzes data collected from over 300 member 
18:544:45910:21:21:71:557:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:lenders,  including  banks  and  non-bank  institutions.  The  PayNet  data  base  is the    largest  U.S. 
18:545:46017:21:20:71:543:584:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:database of small business loans, leases, and credit lines, including over 23 million credit contracts 
18:546:46120:20:21:71:429:564:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:and totaling more than $1.4 trillion in loans outstanding as of this writing. 
18:547:46198:21:21:107:554:543:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:The PayNet data consists of a    loan-  level    panel that follows loan contracts over time, and   a 
18:548:46300:21:21:72:547:522:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:borrower-level    panel dataset. The identities of individual borrowers and lenders  were anonymized 
18:549:46401:21:20:72:542:501:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:in the dataset used for this research. The    loan-   level panel includes the lender type—we know 
18:550:46500:20:21:72:543:481:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:whether  the  lender  is  a  bank, a  finance  company,  or  an  online  lender—and various  loan 
18:551:46598:21:21:72:542:460:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:characteristics, including the amount outstanding and maturity. For a smaller subset of loans, we 
18:552:46696:21:20:72:542:439:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:are also able to infer the interest rat e based on the loan’s original principal amount and payment 
18:553:46796:20:21:72:543:419:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:schedule. We infer the interest rate on each loan by computing an internal rate of return based on 
18:554:46895:21:21:72:542:398:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the initial principal amount and the schedule of promised loan repayments. The    borrower-level 
18:555:46992:21:20:72:543:377:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:panel includes the county where a borrower is located, a borrower’s proprietary credit score from 
18:556:47090:20:21:72:543:357:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:PayNet, and various proxies for   borrower size based on its total    borrowings in the PayNet database. 
18:557:47194:21:21:108:543:336:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Since    all of our regressions are run at the county-year level, the PayNet data is aggregated 
18:558:47290:21:20:72:548:315:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:from   the loan-quarter or borrower-quarter level to the county-year level by taking equ al-weighted 
18:559:47391:20:21:72:543:295:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:averages. To ensure comparability with the CRA data, which defines small business loans as those 
18:560:47487:21:21:72:555:274:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:under $1 million  , we restrict attention to borrowers whose total outstanding loans in the PayNet 
18:561:47586:21:33:72:514:253:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:database (potentially across multiple loans) are less than $2 million at a given point in time. 
18:562:47682:33:20:108:278:220:144:Times:144:Times:A:B. Initial presence of Top 4 banks 
18:563:47716:20:21:108:543:200:144:g_d0_f2:144:Times:A:Our main proxy for the initial presence of Top 4 banks in a given county is the Top  4  
18:564:47804:21:21:72:543:179:144:Times:144:g_d0_f2:B:Deposit  Share or T4DSc. T4DSc is defined as the fraction of county c’s total 2005 deposits that 
18:565:47901:21:20:72:543:158:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:were held at depository institutions owned by Bank of America, Citigroup, JPMorgan, and Wells 
18:566:47995:20:21:72:542:138:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Fargo—i.e., we always aggregate bank-level data to the bank holding company level. T4DSc is 
18:567:48087:21:21:72:543:117:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:constructed by aggregating branch-level data on deposits from the FDIC’s Summary of Deposits 
18:568:48180:21:0:72:542:96:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:(SOD) database to the county level. To ensure that our findings are driven by real changes in bank 
19:569:48282:0:20:72:543:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:behavior as opposed to changes in the ownership structure of banks, we adjust both our CRA and 
19:570:48377:20:21:72:192:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:SOD data for mergers.15 
19:571:48400:21:21:108:565:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Because the CRA database contains  bank   -county level observations on small business loan 
19:572:48492:21:20:72:543:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:originations, we   can also    measure the Top 4’s initial presence in a county using their share of 2005 
19:573:48598:20:21:72:542:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:originations as opposed to their share of deposits. Naturally, the Top 4 loan and deposit shares are 
19:574:48699:21:21:72:557:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:highly correlated across counties—the correlation is 0.75—and we obtain similar results if we   use 
19:575:48799:21:20:72:273:584:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:this alternative proxy for Top 4 presence. 
19:576:48842:20:21:108:542:564:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Nonetheless,  the  Top  4  deposit  share is  our  preferred  measure for  two  reasons. First, 
19:577:48938:21:21:72:558:543:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:because the   FDIC’s deposit data   covers all depository institutions but   the CRA loan data only 
19:578:49038:21:21:72:547:522:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:covers those with assets over $1 billion, our deposit-based measure accounts  for the market share 
19:579:49137:21:20:72:543:501:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:of small community banks with assets less than $1 billion—a set of banks known to play an 
19:580:49227:20:21:72:558:481:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:important role in small business lending (Berger and Udell [2006]). Second, the loan share vari  able 
19:581:49329:21:21:72:540:460:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:may    contain considerable transitory noise which would lead to measurement error in our key right-
19:582:49429:21:20:72:543:439:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:hand side variable. Indeed, the deposit share is more persistent than the loan share, both within 
19:583:49527:20:33:72:222:419:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:counties and across counties.16 
19:584:49558:33:21:108:303:386:144:Times:144:Times:A:C. County-level labor market outcomes 
19:585:49595:21:20:108:543:365:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:We use four measures of county-level labor market activity: the establishment expansion 
19:586:49683:20:21:71:542:345:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:rate,  the  unemployment  rate,  total  employment, and  wages.  We  obtain  county-level  data  on 
19:587:49783:21:21:71:543:324:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:establishment expansion rates—the fraction of business establishments that expand employment 
19:588:49876:21:20:71:543:303:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:in a given year—from the Census’s Bureau’s Statistics on U.S. Businesses (SUSB) database.17 
19:589:49967:20:37:72:543:283:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Second, we obtain annual data on county-level unemployment rates and the size of a county’s 
19:590:50059:37:19:72:219:246:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:                                                 
19:591:50108:19:15:72:544:227:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:15 W e consider any depository institution that was acquired by one of the Top 4 banking firms between 2005 and 2014 
19:592:50225:15:11:72:542:212:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:to be a Top 4 bank in 2005. Thus,    the wave of acquisitions that occurred during the 2008 peak of the financial crisis 
19:593:50346:11:12:72:542:201:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:contributes to the Top 4 share. For example, both Wachovia’s and Washington Mutual’s 2005 deposits contribute to 
19:594:50459:12:11:72:544:189:100:Times:100:g_d0_f2:F:T4DS because the former was acquired by Wells Fargo and the latter was acquired by JPMorgan.  The implicit 
19:595:50565:11:12:72:542:178:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:assumption here is that these acquired banks were impacted by an organization-wide decision to pull back from small 
19:596:50681:12:10:71:187:166:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:business lending after 2008. 
19:597:50709:10:15:72:542:156:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:16 When we instead use the Top 4 loan share, our reduced-form results are slightly weaker, consistent with the view 
19:598:50825:15:11:71:542:141:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:that the loan share is a noisier measure of a county’s exposure to the Top 4 than the deposit share. However, we obtain 
19:599:50945:11:12:71:542:130:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:statistically strong and economically larger results if we use the deposit share as an instrument for the loan share. This 
19:600:51068:12:11:71:542:118:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:approach is the natural solution to eliminating the attenuation bias resulting from the fact that the loan share is 
19:601:51184:11:10:71:157:107:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:measured with error. 
19:602:51204:10:15:72:542:97:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:17 The SUSB is carried out on March 12th each year. We call the expansion rate from March 12, YYYY to March 12, 
19:603:51316:15:0:72:527:82:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:YYYY+1 the “year-YYYY expansion rate.” The SUSB data is currently only available through 2012–2013.     
20:604:51423:0:20:72:543:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:civilian  labor  force  from  the  Bureau  of  Labor  Statistics’  Local  Area  Unemployment  (LAU) 
20:605:51523:20:21:72:543:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:database. Our annual county-level LAU data reflect the annual average of 12 monthly surveys for 
20:606:51619:21:21:72:543:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:each county. Third, we obtain annual data on county-level total private employment and wages 
20:607:51712:21:20:72:540:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:from the BLS Quarterly Census of Employment and Wages (QCEW) database. Our annual county-
20:608:51801:20:21:71:542:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:level QCEW data on private employment reflect the annual average of four quarterly QCEW 
20:609:51889:21:21:71:543:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:surveys for each county. Our wage variable is the annual average pay per employee, which the 
20:610:51982:21:33:71:540:584:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Census computes by dividing total annual wages by annual average employment in each county.  
20:611:52075:33:20:107:283:551:144:Times:144:Times:A:D. Additional county-level controls 
20:612:52110:20:21:107:542:531:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Our difference-in-difference specifications control for a number of additional county-level 
20:613:52202:21:21:71:542:510:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:variables. First,  we  use  the  QCEW  data  to  compute  the  distribution  of  2005  county-level 
20:614:52302:21:20:71:543:489:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:employment across nine    broad industries.  We include these county-level   employment shares as 
20:615:52400:20:21:71:543:469:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:controls to ensure that our results are not driven by the possibility that counties with a high 
20:616:52496:21:21:71:542:448:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:exposure  to  the  Top  4  banks  had  different  exposures  to  common  industry  shocks  than  other 
20:617:52599:21:20:71:117:427:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:counties. 
20:618:52609:20:21:107:547:407:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Second, to control for potential differences in local fundamentals  linked to demographics, 
20:619:52701:21:21:72:542:386:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:we obtain 2005 county-level demographic information from the American Community Survey 
20:620:52788:21:20:72:542:365:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:(ACS), including the fraction of the population that is college-educated, the homeownership rate, 
20:621:52886:20:21:71:533:345:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the fraction of the population aged 25 years or older, and the fraction of the population over 65. 
20:622:52985:21:21:107:543:324:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Finally, we control for county-level home price appreciation from 2002 to 2006, which we 
20:623:53074:21:20:71:542:303:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:compute by taking a population-weighted average within each county of zip-code level home price 
20:624:53170:20:21:71:542:283:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:data    from Zillow. We control for 2002–2006 home price appreciation because those   counties with 
20:625:53270:21:21:71:543:262:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the most rapid appreciation over this period subsequently saw the largest decline in house prices 
20:626:53368:21:21:71:543:241:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:from 2006 to 2010 (Mian and Sufi [2016]), which in turn impacted local demand and economic 
20:627:53459:21:20:71:412:220:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:activity via a household net worth channel as in Mian and Sufi (2014). 
20:628:53530:20:14:71:74:200:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B: 
20:629:53530:14:21:107:531:186:144:g_d0_f4:144:g_d0_f4:A:V. The Effect of the Small Business Credit Supply on Local Economic Activity 
20:630:53605:21:20:107:543:165:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:We now examine the economic consequences of the   shock to the supply of small business 
20:631:53693:20:21:71:542:145:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:loans from   the Top 4 banks. Our   basic empirical strategy is a difference-in-difference approach 
20:632:53793:21:21:71:542:124:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:that compares economic outcomes in counties with a high Top 4 share to those in otherwise similar 
20:633:53891:21:0:71:548:103:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:counties with a low Top 4 share. W e first   present baseline difference-in-difference estimates of  the 
21:634:53999:0:20:72:542:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:initial impact of this credit supply shock on local credit and labor markets from 2006 to 2010. To 
21:635:54098:20:21:72:596:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:understand how affected counties have adjusted over time, we then   trace    out   the dynamic impact 
21:636:54200:21:21:72:543:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:over    our full 2006 to 2014 sample. Next, we   present three    separate triple-difference specifications 
21:637:54308:21:20:72:557:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:that  help  to  isolate  the underlying economic  mechanism via    which  this  credit  supply  shock 
21:638:54410:20:21:72:543:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:impacted local labor markets. Finally, we use our data from PayNet to better understand how local 
21:639:54508:21:33:72:310:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:credit markets have adjusted to the supply shock. 
21:640:54558:33:21:108:492:572:144:Times:144:Times:A:A. Baseline difference-in-difference results: Initial impact on affected counties 
21:641:54639:21:20:108:389:551:144:Times:144:Times:A:A.1. First stage estimates of the impact on loan volume

21:650:55355:21:21:72:542:356:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:In other words, equation (3) is a difference-in-difference specification that compares the change

22:690:58985:19:15:72:542:132:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:19 O ur baseline measure of county-level loan originations includes all small business loans with initial balances less 
22:691:59105:15:11:71:542:117:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:than $1 million. The CRA database also contains data on loan originations to very small firms with annual revenues 
22:692:59220:11:13:71:545:106:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:less than $1 million. We obtain nearly identical results using this narrower measure. For example,  if we use this 
22:693:59335:13:11:71:554:93:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:narrower measure, the coefficient on T4DSc in the specification corresponding to column (5) of Table 3 is β1 = –16.9   
22:694:59454:11:0:71:167:82:100:g_d0_f2:100:Times:F:with a t-statistic of 3.6. 
23:695:59483:0:20:108:528:708:144:Times:144:Times:A:A.2. Reduced-form and instrumental-variables estimates of impact on labor markets 
23:696:59564:20:21:108:543:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:We now turn to our reduced-form   results, which show that counties with a higher initial 
23:697:59654:21:21:72:542:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Top 4 share also experienced   more adverse labor market outcomes from 2006 to 2010. We begin 
23:698:59748:21:20:72:542:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:by examining the impact on the expansion rate of business establishments,  which is arguably our 
23:699:59845:20:21:72:543:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:best measure of small business activity in a county because it counts all establishments equally. 
23:700:59943:21:21:72:546:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Indeed, small business owners report that a lack of access to credit primarily leads them to  scale 
23:701:60043:21:20:72:500:584:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:back the rate at which they are expanding their businesses (Mills and McCarthy [2014]). 
23:702:60131:20:21:108:543:564:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:The impact of the Top 4 credit supply shock on establishment expansion rates is shown in 
23:703:60220:21:21:72:542:543:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Panel B of    Figure 3. As can be seen, there is a robust negative relationship between the change in 
23:704:60322:21:21:72:543:522:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:a county’s expansion rate from 2006 to 2010 and the county’s Top 4 Deposit Share in 2005. The 
23:705:60416:21:20:72:542:501:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:corresponding  reduced-form regressions  are reported  in   Panel  A  of Table 4.  Specifically,  we 
23:706:60517:20:28:72:369:481:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:estimate county-level cross-sectional regressions of the form: 
23:707:60579:28:22:196:543:453:58:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:2224,ccccExpansionsT   DSαβξ′∆=+×   +  +γx (4) 
23:708:60625:22:22:72:542:431:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:where ∆Expansionsc is the change in the county-level establishment expansion rate from 2006 to 
23:709:60720:22:20:72:542:409:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:2010. The coefficient on T4DSc of  –1.59 in column (3) implies that a county with a 100% Top 4 
23:710:60815:20:21:72:543:389:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:share saw a 1.59 percentage point decline in the establishment expansion rate relative to a county 
23:711:60914:21:21:72:543:368:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:with no Top 4 presence. Put   differently, a one standard deviation increase in T4DSc is associated 
23:712:61014:21:20:72:483:347:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:with  a 0.158 (= 1.59 × 0.230 ÷ 2.31) standard deviation decline in the expansion rate. 
23:713:61102:20:21:107:560:327:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Relative to column (1), columns (2)  through (4) add the same batteries of controls that    we 
23:714:61197:21:21:72:542:306:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:introduced  in  Table  3. Column  (5)  in  Table  4  adds  the  lagged  outcome  variable—the  2005 
23:715:61297:21:20:72:543:285:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:establishment expansion rate—as a control. Controlling for pre-trends in this way is an important 
23:716:61395:20:21:72:543:265:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:robustness check in a difference-in-difference design. If the outcome variable is mean-reverting 
23:717:61492:21:21:72:543:244:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:and the treated and untreated counties differ in their average initial level of the outcome variable, 
23:718:61594:21:21:72:543:223:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:one might mistake mean reversion for a treatment effect (Ashenfelter [1978]). Hence, the parallel 
23:719:61692:21:20:72:543:202:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:trends assumption is more credible when controlling for the lagged outcome, as we do in column 
23:720:61787:20:21:72:542:182:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:(5).   In summary, the estimates from columns (2) through (5) show that   introducing a large battery 
23:721:61889:21:21:71:341:161:144:g_d0_f2:64:g_d0_f2:B:of  controls has little effect on the coefficient of interest. 
23:722:61951:21:20:108:563:140:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Panel B of Table 4 presents the    corresponding instrumental-variables (IV)    estimates. We 
23:723:62045:20:25:71:306:120:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:estimate cross-sectional regressions of the form: 
23:724:62095:25:0:241:543:95:174:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:%,cIVIVcIVccExpansionsLoansαβω′∆= + ×∆    +   +γx (5) 
24:725:62151:0:22:72:562:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:using T4DSc as an instrument for %∆Loansc. Thus   , the point estimates in Panel B of Table 4 are 
24:726:62249:22:21:72:542:686:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:simply the ratio of the coefficients on T4DSc from    the reduced form in Panel A and first stage in 
24:727:62350:21:21:72:545:665:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Table 3—i.e., 훽훽퐼퐼퐼퐼=훽훽2/훽훽1.  Focusing on column (3), our IV estimates suggest that a credit supply 
24:728:62451:21:22:72:546:644:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:shock  that  leads  to  a  one-standard  deviation decline in  %∆Loansc leads  to  a  0.610  
24:729:62544:22:21:71:543:622:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:(=0.0766 × 18.4 ÷ 2.31) standard deviation fall  in ∆Expansionsc. These estimates support the view 
24:730:62643:21:21:71:496:601:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:that credit supply shocks can have a meaningful impact on local small business activity. 
24:731:62731:21:21:107:542:580:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:The key identifying assumption underpinning our difference-in-difference estimates is that 
24:732:62822:21:21:71:542:559:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:high and low Top 4 bank counties would have followed parallel trends in the absence of the credit 
24:733:62920:21:20:71:566:538:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:supply shock from the Top 4 banks. To assess the plausibility this  assumption, Figure 4 plots    the 
24:734:63022:20:21:71:542:518:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:time  -series dynamics  of annual loan originations and establishment expansion rates in high and 
24:735:63120:21:21:71:542:497:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:low Top 4 counties. Figure 4 shows that loan originations and expansion rates in high and low Top 
24:736:63218:21:20:71:542:476:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:4 counties followed roughly paral  lel  paths from 1999 through 2007. However, beginning in 2008, 
24:737:63316:20:21:71:542:456:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:establishment expansion rates in high Top 4 counties fall significantly relative to those in low Top 
24:738:63417:21:21:71:482:435:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:4 counties—just as loan originations in high and low Top 4 counties diverge sharply. 
24:739:63502:21:20:107:542:414:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Although the Top 4 banks were growing their   small business lending more rapidly than 
24:740:63589:20:21:71:542:394:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:other banks before 2008, Figure 4 shows that the growth in total    small business lending by all 
24:741:63687:21:21:71:543:373:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:banks was similar in high and low Top 4 counties prior to the crisis. This is because the Top 4 
24:742:63783:21:21:71:543:352:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:banks were    rapidly gaining market share at the expense of other banks in these areas. Thus, judged 
24:743:63885:21:20:71:542:331:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:relative to low Top 4 counties, it does not appear that aggregate small business lending conditions 
24:744:63985:20:21:71:542:311:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:were    overheated in high Top 4 counties before the crisis. To be sure, this fact does not allow us to 
24:745:64089:21:21:71:543:290:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:conclude that the pre-crisis level of small business lending by the Top 4 was not excessive in some 
24:746:64189:21:20:71:556:269:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:way  ; for example, it may have been excessive relative to their own underwriting capabilities in 
24:747:64287:20:21:71:543:249:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:this  segment.     However,  the  evidence does  cut  against  the  view  that  high  Top  4  counties 
24:748:64390:21:21:71:543:228:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:experienced  worse  credit  and  labor  market outcomes beginning  in  2008  simply  because the 
24:749:64487:21:20:71:543:207:144:Times:144:g_d0_f2:B:aggregate quantity of   small business credit had been particularly over-extended in those areas and 
24:750:64588:20:21:71:379:187:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:they were therefore experiencing a larger post-crisis correction. 
24:751:64653:21:22:107:542:166:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Table 5 presents analogous results for three other county-level labor market outcomes:

25:770:66284:27:20:107:258:367:144:Times:144:Times:A:A.3. Aggregate implications 
25:771:66311:20:21:107:542:347:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Looking across counties, the results in Tables 4 and 5 suggest that the shock to the supply 
25:772:66403:21:21:71:543:326:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:of small business credit from the Top 4 banks had a significant initial impact on local labor markets 
25:773:66505:21:21:71:545:305:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:from 2006 to 2010. Did this credit supply shock from Top 4 banks have a meaningful effect on  the 
25:774:66603:21:20:71:548:284:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:national unemployment rate from 2006 to 2010? While we cannot account for any  potential general 
25:775:66700:20:21:71:562:264:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:equilibrium effects stemming from the Top 4 bank credit supply contraction, we can offer    a rough 
25:776:66800:21:21:71:543:243:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:back -of-the-envelope calculation  based  on  our  cross-sectional  micro-estimates. Since  the 
25:777:66896:21:20:71:556:222:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:population-weighted average level of T4DS is 30%, our   reduced-form   estimates from column (3) 
25:778:66993:20:22:71:542:202:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:of Table 5 Panel A suggest that exposure to the Top 4 banks directly contributed 0.3 p.p. (= 30% 
25:779:67090:22:21:72:543:180:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:× 0.93 p.p.) to the rise in the national unemployment rate between 2006 to 2010. Because the 
25:780:67183:21:0:72:543:159:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:unemployment rate rose by 5.1 p.p. over this period, this suggests that the Top 4 credit supply 
26:781:67282:0:20:72:542:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:shock accounts for roughly 5% of the total increase.20 Obviously, this calculation should be taken 
26:782:67381:20:21:72:543:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:with a healthy grain of salt. However, it suggests that the Top 4 credit supply shock may have had 
26:783:67480:21:21:72:240:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:non-trivial aggregate implications. 
26:784:67515:21:20:108:543:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Going further, if one believes that part of the broader decline in the quantity of small 
26:785:67604:20:21:72:554:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:business lending reflects  a generalized contraction in bank   loan supply, then an extrapolation of 
26:786:67705:21:21:72:542:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:our difference-in-difference results suggests that the resulting small business credit gap may have 
26:787:67805:21:20:72:543:584:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:contributed significantly to  the  severity  of  the  Great  Recession  and  the  sluggish  pace  of  the 
26:788:67911:20:21:72:543:564:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:recovery. For instance, suppose that one believes that one-   third  of the overall 42 p.p. decline in 
26:789:68014:21:21:72:543:543:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:small business lending from 2006 to 2010 was  driven by a contraction in credit supply. Then our 
26:790:68111:21:21:72:543:522:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:IV estimates from column (3) of Table 5 Panel B would suggest that the resulting small business 
26:791:68207:21:20:72:542:501:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:credit  gap could  explain  14%  (=  1/3  ×  –0.0525 ×  –42  ÷  5.1)  of  the  rise  in  the  national 
26:792:68310:20:33:72:236:481:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:unemployment over this period.21 
26:793:68342:33:21:108:521:448:144:Times:144:Times:A:B. Dynamics: How local economic activity adjusted to the Top 4 credit supply shock 
26:794:68424:21:20:108:542:427:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Next, we explore the dynamic impact on   local    credit and labor market activity following 
26:795:68517:20:21:72:565:407:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the initial shock to Top 4 loan supply in 2008. What    adjustment process might one expect to see if 
26:796:68619:21:21:72:543:386:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the Top 4 banks pulled back from small business lending and never really returned? Initially, the 
26:797:68717:21:20:72:543:365:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:negative supply shock should lead to a small business credit crunch with attendant negative effects 
26:798:68817:20:21:72:540:345:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:on local employment, just as we saw in the prior section. Over time, however, other lenders—
26:799:68909:21:21:72:542:324:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:either small banks or non-bank lenders—should be drawn into the market by the promise of greater 
26:800:69006:21:20:72:543:303:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:returns, leading to a more normalized flow of credit in affected counties. However, to the extent 
26:801:69104:20:21:72:546:283:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:that    these new lenders were  higher cost providers of credit than the Top 4 banks, the n the supply 
26:802:69207:21:21:72:543:262:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:shock might have a long-lasting impact on the cost of credit. Turning to the labor market, as the 
26:803:69305:21:21:72:559:241:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:acute credit shortage eases and real    wages slowly adjust downwards, one would expect the   adverse 
26:804:69407:21:23:72:562:220:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:effects on employment to dissipate. However, if the    cost of small business credit remains elevated 
26:805:69509:23:18:72:219:197:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:                                                 
26:806:69558:18:15:72:542:179:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:20 Based on Table 1, on a population-weighted basis, the unemployment rose by 5.1 p.p. in the average county. This 
26:807:69673:15:12:71:542:164:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:closely tracks the rise in the national unemployment rate of 4.9 p.p. from 4.4% in December 2006 to 9.3% in December 
26:808:69790:12:10:71:116:152:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:2010.     
26:809:69800:10:15:72:542:142:42:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:21 If we instead use the   somewhat larger estimates in column (2), we would calculate that exposure to the Top 4 banks 
26:810:69920:15:11:72:542:127:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:directly contributed 0.7 p.p. (= 30% × 2.4 p.p.) to the rise in the national unemployment rate or roughly 14% of the 
26:811:70037:11:12:72:542:116:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:total increase between 2006 and 2010. And our extrapolation based on our IV estimates would suggest that a broader 
26:812:70152:12:0:72:507:104:100:g_d0_f2:100:g_d0_f2:F:small business credit gap could explain 37% (= 1/3 × – 0.134 × –42 ÷ 5.1) of the total rise in unemployment. 
27:813:70263:0:20:72:543:708:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:in affected areas, small businesses in these areas might become less capital intensive, leading to 
27:814:70362:20:21:72:231:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:persistently lower local wages.22 
27:815:70395:21:21:108:543:667:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:To trace out the cumulative response of county-level outcomes following the initial shock, 
27:816:70486:21:20:72:543:646:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Table  6  adapt   s  our  baseline  difference-in-difference  methodology. Specifically,  for  a  given 
27:817:70590:20:21:72:543:626:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:outcome variable Yct, we use a county-year panel from 2006 to 2014 and estimate regressions of

29:885:76715:21:33:71:319:605:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:product of labor and, hence, on equilibrium wages. 
29:886:76766:33:20:107:245:572:144:Times:144:Times:A:C. Isolating the mechanism 
29:887:76792:20:21:107:543:552:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:In  this subsection,  we  assess  the  extent  to  which  a  county’s  initial  Top  4  exposure 
29:888:76889:21:21:71:542:531:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:influenced county-level employment through a narrow small business credit supply channel or 
29:889:76981:21:21:71:542:510:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:through a broader credit supply channel. As   we noted above, while the Top 4 banks’ cutback in 
29:890:77077:21:20:72:557:489:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:small business credit was especially pronounced, their   loan growth has been stagnant in many 
29:891:77172:20:21:71:542:469:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:categories since 2007. Thus, in addition to cutbacks in small business credit, a county’s exposure 
29:892:77271:21:21:71:543:448:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:to  the Top  4  banks  may  have affected  local  labor  markets because it  reduced  the  supply  of 
29:893:77373:21:20:72:543:427:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:household credit, thereby   crimping local consumer demand.24 Although we cannot rule out the 
29:894:77467:20:21:72:542:407:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:existence of  this broader credit channel, we present three triple-difference specifications which 
29:895:77566:21:21:72:543:386:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:collectively suggest that a narrower small business credit channel plays an important role in driving 
29:896:77668:21:26:72:179:365:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:our baseline findings.

33:1001:87024:20:21:72:543:688:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:price declines from 2007 to 2009 led to   larger declines in local employment in non-tradable

33:1006:87505:21:20:71:543:584:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:housing-related effect documented in Mian and Sufi (2014), but, because small firms in tradable

35:1074:93563:21:21:71:542:584:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:this equation using two -stage least squares on the cross-section of differences from 2006 to 2010, 
35:1075:93663:21:21:71:543:563:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:with 푇푇4퐷퐷퐷퐷푏푏 serving as instrument for the   change in interest rate Δ푟푟푏푏. Thus, the cross-sectional 
35:1076:93767:21:21:72:546:542:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:analogue to Tabl   e 10 is  the first stage regression,  and the regression in Table 2 is  the reduced form. 
35:1077:93876:21:20:72:543:521:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:Estimating this    semi   -elasticity provides another sanity check on the analysis: we want to know 
35:1078:93976:20:21:72:543:501:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:whether  a  plausible  semi-elasticity  of  demand  can  be  used  to  reconcile  our  findings on  loan 
35:1079:94081:21:21:72:257:480:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:quantities with our findings on prices. 
35:1080:94121:21:21:108:542:459:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:Columns (1) and (2) of Table 11 present these    results. I n column (1), we estimate that the 
35:1081:94216:21:21:72:543:438:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:semi   -elasticity of loan demand is β = –19.8 p.p. In other words, a 100 basis point increase in the 
35:1082:94318:21:21:71:542:417:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:cost of credit leads to a 20 p.p. decline in demand. The estimates are imprecise, which is hardly 
35:1083:94416:21:21:71:543:396:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:surprising given    the large number of other changes in credit markets  over this time period as well 
35:1084:94519:21:21:71:543:375:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:as the coarseness of the data  . However, the magnitude of the estimated semi-elasticity of demand 
35:1085:94618:21:20:71:543:354:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:seems reasonable, suggesting that the decline in lending volumes we observe can plausibly be tied 
35:1086:94716:20:27:71:218:334:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:to the increased cost of credit. 
35:1087:94749:27:21:107:281:307:144:Times:144:Times:A:D.2. The response of other banks 
35:1088:94781:21:20:107:543:286:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:A:In order to study the response of other banks to the pullback in small business lending by 
35:1089:94872:20:21:71:542:266:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the Top 4 banks, we decompose total county loan growth by all banks (A) into a component from 
35:1090:94966:21:21:71:542:245:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:the Top 4 banks (T4), from other big  banks (B) with    2005 assets between $50  and $500 billion, 
35:1091:95065:21:26:71:381:224:144:g_d0_f2:144:g_d0_f2:B:and from small banks (S)  with  2005 assets under $50 billion: 
35:1092:95128:26:20:129:247:198:53:g_d0_f2:53:g_d0_f2:?:,14,1,1,1
